Secondly, to the Iranians, Americans and Qataris Israeli civilian lives are fair game but American and Qatari lives are not. If an American or Qatari had died from an Iranian missile, despite the Iranians doing everything they could to avoid it, the American response would have been severe. Thirdly, and this ties into the Mission Accomplished ceasefire announcement, this was the moment the Americans attempted to extricate themselves from the conflict as if the bombing of the Iranian nuclear sites had never happened. I speculated in the previous paragraph that the Americans and Israelis after the bombing of the nuclear sites were totally aligned and this was effectively now a joint operation. This seems to have been premature. The American mission, to use American stealth bombers and bunker busting bombs to neutralize Iranian nuclear sites may very well have been accomplished. I find it fanciful now though that the Israelis will settle for any military objective(s) other than totally wiping out Iran's ability to fire missiles at Israel (at the time of writing over half of Iran's missile launchers have been destroyed and Israel continues to control Iranian skies) and sparking a regime change after decades of terrorism, chaos and death funded and supported by the Iranian regime. Mission accomplished for the Americans, perhaps. Mission incomplete for the Israelis, almost certainly.

"We basically have two countries that have been fighting so long and so hard that they don't know what the f\*\*\* they're doing." President Trump

In the fog of war it is impossible to know what is authentic and what is misdirection. After what was pulled off prior to the first Israeli strikes and the American strikes anything is possible. On the face of it Trump is angry with the Israelis and there is a split between the Americans and the Israelis over whether it is mission accomplished or not. But if the Americans wanted to extricate themselves from the war and position themselves once more as a quasi neutral mediator this is exactly the sort of message they would be sending publicly. Regardless of whether the anger is authentic or yet another ruse nothing will take away from what Trump and the Americans have achieved in recent days. It is truly historic. From my perspective both the Americans and the Israelis are doing exactly what they should be doing assuming their objectives aren't in perfect alignment. The Israelis want to put a stop to Iranian missiles once and for all. After all the Israeli casualties over the years you can hardly blame them. Any end state that results in more Iranian missiles fired at Israeli civilians in the coming months or years, via Iranian skies that today are controlled by the Israelis, is unacceptable to them. The Americans are prioritizing preventing the war from spiralling and minimizing the chances of it needing further American intervention. Assuming Trump's anger is authentic one hopes the Americans and Israelis can smooth over their differences and see the other side's perspective. Assuming Trump's anger is yet another example of misdirection I've been fooled yet again. It certainly isn't the first time in this war and it won't be the last.

## 69 Threading the needle on a Middle Eastern peace deal

On June 27nd 2025 the ceasefire brokered, announced and defended verbally in the sternest of terms by President Trump has held for two days after what appeared to be initial breaches. Each day that passes cements the American extrication from involvement in direct hostilities which seems to have been the primary American objective post the bombing of the Iranian nuclear sites. It is speculated that Netanyahu and Trump are working on a plan to end the war in Gaza and expand the Abraham Accords (Times of Israel). Satisfying Israeli objectives is going to be much more complex and multi-layered than satisfying the American objective. I discussed earlier the Israeli tendency to follow up emphatic military victories with weak political surrenders including after the Six Day War in 1967. In that case the political surrender and the status quo implemented on the Temple Mount ended up lasting for decades. If this indeed was a Twelve Day War approximately 50 years after the Six Day War what is needed to prevent the need for a Eighteen Day War in another 50 years? And many more wars and Israeli civilian and soldier deaths in the intervening period? What are the expectations of a serious nation state like say the United States with centuries of history? A serious nation state knows its borders and exerts sovereignty within those borders. It doesn't have to go to global organizations like the United Nations and justify why it doesn't form new nation states within those borders especially when it only controls a land mass similar in size to New Jersey. It doesn't let foreign nations and foreign religions dictate how the center of its capital/Capitol is governed. If a foreign nation fires a missile into its borders it immediately declares war on that foreign nation and has allies that will support it verbally and/or militarily to ensure no further missiles are fired at it. It doesn't shrug its shoulders and wait another 50 years to prevent it happening again. Is this the moment Israel becomes a serious nation state like say the United States, obviously without the global authority and military might of a (pre-eminent) superpower, or is this yet another stepping stone and opportunity missed to become a serious nation state? Is this the moment killing an Israeli civilian or soldier becomes as consequential as killing an American or Qatari? Or will Israelis continue to be cannon fodder for another 50 years as the price they have to pay for living in the Middle East? It isn't impossible that Trump may still thread the needle on a lasting Middle Eastern peace deal. But whether Israel and Netanyahu make political surrenders (yet again) is a different question entirely.

One of the technological miracles post internet is that with the permission of the participants (or perhaps without if you're the CIA or Mossad) you can hear conversations that you would never have been able to hear pre internet. In some cases you can hear those conversations live as they happen. Pre internet you would have needed to have obtained the permission of a radio station or TV channel to beam a conversation to a larger audience. Post internet generally (there are counterexamples with banning, shadowbanning and suppressing freedom of reach of course) conversations can be beamed to a larger audience without needing the permission of a particular radio station or TV channel. Living in this post internet era I have been able to listen in on conversations I would have never been able to listen in on in a pre internet era. One particular conversation I have been listening to intently over the past year or so is the conversation between former American spy Jonathan Pollard and Rabbi David Bar-Hayim on the Machon Shilo YouTube channel or when YouTube is being particularly censorship trigger happy the much less censorship trigger happy Rumble channel. Jonathan Pollard served 30 years in a US prison for violating the Espionage Act and handing over classified US intelligence to the Israelis. Bar-Hayim has spent 20 years building the Shilo Institute for the "research, elucidation and dissemination of the Torah of Israel" (Wikipedia). In the worlds of intelligence services and rabbinic Judaism, of which until more recently I knew very little, it has given me an insight into what these communities might be thinking on various topics that wouldn't typically get covered on the mainstream media. One of the topics they've covered extensively is their frustrations that they've held for many years with both Netanyahu and the Israeli "juristocracy" for keeping Israel's democratic system in a metaphorical straitjacket guaranteeing terrible outcomes for the Israeli electorate. In a recent conversation they discussed Netanyahu's embrace of Judaism and G\*d rather late in life and whether it is authentic or merely politically convenient. There is an interesting parallel with President Trump's recent embrace of Christianity and G\*d rather late in life post an assassination attempt at a political rally in Pennsylvania in which a bullet grazed his ear. I described Trump's earlier decision on whether to bomb Iranian nuclear sites as a choice of whether to put his chips on Bibi and Israel. In setting out his position on what is acceptable for Israel in upcoming negotiations we'll see if Bibi is willing to put his chips on Judaism and G\*d. What does G\*d want for Israel in the next 50 years and beyond? Does G\*d want 50 more years of uncertainty, chaos and suffering because sovereignty over Jewish lands and its holiest sites was left ambiguous or worse given away? Another 50 years of Arabs killing Jews and Jews killing Arabs because Jews can't decide whether they deserve full sovereignty over a relatively small strip of land in the Middle East? Or does the Torah outline a different path?

"Paradoxically the only way G\*d can be revealed is by being concealed. By obscuring the divine light creation allows it to shine... It is the human task through the performance of the commandments and enactment of the divine will to reveal G\*d's presence in the world." Ezra Glinter (biography of Menachem Mendel Schneerson,"The Rebbe")

If Itamar Ben-Gvir wasn't waiting in the wings one would be more anxious about the prospect of Netanyahu caving under American pressure to set Israel on a path to repeat the mistakes of the last 50 years. Just like in Michelangelo's famous "The Creation of Adam" painting G\*d's finger may be outstretched but it requires Adam to unbend and also outstretch his finger to meet G\*d halfway. Ultimately after a 553 page story which no doubt hasn't been pleasant at various points wrestling with everyone from the Israeli juristocracy to multiple American administrations, fixed for whatever reason on Israel being permanently locked in a battle with a non-existent Palestinian state, it would be nice to see Netanyahu be the one to deliver a platform for Israel's future security as a nation state with actualized borders. But if he can't deliver it having Ben-Gvir waiting in the wings as a potential successor, someone who for 30 years has been steadfastly against carving up Jewish lands in a misguided attempt to achieve peace, has taken a much deeper interest in the management of Judaism's holiest site and arguably wears his religion and belief in G\*d with greater ease, offers some significant insurance. Just like President Trump in the United States, Netanyahu's national poll numbers have been repeatedly underestimated and one would assume the same effect applies to other political figures on the right wing such as Ben-Gvir and Bezalel Smotrich. For most of Netanyahu's career he has led coalitions where he was positioned as the most right wing of that coalition but today that is no longer the case. This could get Netanyahu over the finish line for his political legacy with a combination of Netanyahu being less politically exposed and the futility of American pressure to push him out only resulting in an even more right wing coalition. But if it doesn't get him over the finish line there are alternative paths for the divine light to shine through that are already detectable to the human eye.

## 70 Revisiting the intersection or barrier between Judaism and Christianity

"There's an important distinction between the new covenant and the old. There is a new covenant that G\*d made with the Christians and that does supersede the old covenant. But the New Testament doesn't supersede the Old. Because quite frankly if it really did we wouldn't have an Old Testament in the bible. A phrase I learned in Christian philosophy many years ago is that the New Testament is in the Old concealed and the Old Testament is in the New revealed. You see here the intimate relationship between the Old and the New Testament." Dinesh D'Souza (Alex Jones debate with Nick Fuentes)

I stated earlier that the intersection or barrier between Judaism and Christianity is a challenging one. It is not as challenging as the one between Christianity and Islam but it is challenging nonetheless. In Matthew 5:17 Jesus stated "Do not think that I have come to abolish the Law or the Prophets; I have not come to abolish them but to fulfill them." Hence it is difficult to justify the supersessionist Christian belief that the new covenant replaced the old, that the Holy Land lost its holiness overnight, that the Jews should abandon their customs, traditions and 613 commandments or that the Jews shouldn't pine for a rebuilding of their Holy Temple and instead discard the perceived "baggage" of Judaism and convert to Christianity. Unsurprisingly I subscribe to the dispensationalist belief that different peoples have different roles and narrative arcs and it is absurd to think all Jews should convert to Christianity or all Christians should convert to Judaism, especially under the threat of force. Judaism doesn't proselytize whilst Christianity does but that doesn't mean Jews can't respect Christians and vice versa. A Christian proselytizing to a devout Orthodox or Hasidic Jew living an authentic Jewish life in Jerusalem is not the same as that Christian proselytizing to a sinning, despairing atheist in say London. The former already has a deep spiritual life and a connection to G\*d whilst the latter does not. The Christian Church may be the "new Israel" for the Christians but Israel has always just been Israel for the Jews. That's not to say that Christian sites and churches should be demolished within Israel because the Christians have founded their "new Israel" outside of Israel. As stated before it is difficult to see how the modern day nation state of Israel would have come into being without the cooperation of Christians and Jews benefit not only from Christian tourism but also the interest and support evangelical Christians show for Israel from abroad. Similarly, sustaining and visiting the historical Christian sites such as the Church of the Holy Sepulchre in the Old City of Jerusalem where Christians believe Jesus was resurrected breathes life into the Christian faith. The human experience is deeply impacted by experiencing places in the flesh and being able to trace the footsteps of historic and religious figures. No technology from the world's most impressive churches and cathedrals to virtual reality handsets will ever be able to fully replicate that experience. Every day and every generation that passes without the rebuilding of the Holy Temple is another day and another generation that doesn't get to experience the Holy Temple in Jerusalem like Jesus did.

There is some natural mistrust between Jews and Christians dating back to the millennia when the Jews suffered in exile and were scattered "among all peoples, from one end of the earth to the other" (Deuteronomy 28:64). Having lost their lands and being at the mercy of their patrons in foreign lands gave added credence to the notion that G\*d had deserted Jews and they were being punished for not accepting the new covenant and refusing to follow what was essentially a new religion. Even today accusations of rejecting Jesus abound from the supersessionists when it is not clear what "accept" and "reject" mean in this context. If "accept" means identifying Jesus as the Jewish Messiah (Moshiach) and appending the New Testament books to the Torah and Tanakh as Jewish holy books then accepting and not rejecting Jesus essentially means converting to Christianity and ditching Judaism. If "accept" means identifying that a Jew called Jesus existed and bore a new religion that the vast majority of Jews don't follow as their religious practices existed prior to Jesus then I suspect large swathes of Jews do "accept" Jesus. Regardless being taken from the nations and being brought back into their own land and the land of their ancestors (Ezekiel 36:24, Ezekiel 37:21, Jeremiah 16:15 etc) presents a significant challenge to the supersessionists and perhaps partly explains the bile and hysteria that is directed towards the modern day nation state of Israel. A rather bizarre alliance of supersessionist Christians, Muslim extremists and atheists with completely disparate belief systems share next to nothing in common apart from a shared interest in not wanting to see the restoration of the "fortunes of my people Israel and Judah" (Jeremiah 30:3). However, the modern day nation state of Israel merely existing if not thriving significantly strengthens the hand of the non-supersessionist Christians and presents an opportunity for Jews and Christians to turn the page on a volatile and oftentimes ugly chapter of co-existence. Now the asymmetry of Christians having their own lands and Jews not has been corrected and biblical prophecy seems to be being fulfilled one would hope the next millennia of relations would be less fraught.

## 71 Oil and water: Why Islamic and Judeo-Christian civilizations do not mix

The United States showed in the 20th century that a Judeo-Christian civilization could not only function but thrive and dominate. Although there will always be theological disagreements between Jews and Christians on the divinity of the New Testament books and whether Jesus was the Jewish Messiah or not that didn't prevent the United States from becoming the pre-eminent superpower, the most formidable military power, the most innovative technological power and the most admired cultural force. As a minority American Jews outperformed relative to their small number (approximately 5 million in 1950 rising to approximately 6 million in 1990) in various fields from finance, law, medicine to the creative arts but to the extent that Judaism clashed with Christianity, rather than merely sprouting it, Jews did not try to impose Judaism on Christian societies and accepted that as a small minority in exile they flourished only under the patronage and consent of the Christian majority. They certainly did not convert Christian churches into Jewish synagogues or worse bulldoze them to build synagogues on top of them, they did not have billions of Jews waiting in the wings to migrate into the United States and fundamentally change the civilization that had been built there, they did not carry out a multitude of terrorist attacks culminating in the Twin Towers attack on 9/11 and they (generally) didn't ally with socialist and communist movements to overturn the capitalistic nature of the United States' economy. To be short American Jews were broadly happy to operate, compete and contribute within the American system rather than attempting to overturn or destroy it. Although no (minority) population is perfect the United States may look back on its Jewish minority population in the 20th century as the gold standard for how a minority population can and should operate as other minority populations swell in number in the 21st century to far beyond the size of the Jewish minority in the 20th century. That's when we're really start to see why, despite their differences, Judeo-Christian civilizations function and don't try to destroy the other in a way that other paired civilizations do not.

"The new rulers of Cambodia call 1975 Year Zero, the dawn of an age in which there will be no families, no sentiment, no expressions of love or grief, no medicines, no hospitals, no schools, no books, no learning, no holidays, no music, no song, no post, no money - only work and death." John Pilger (Year Zero: The Silent Death of Cambodia)

What Rabbi Meir Kahane recognized and what he was legally crucified for and ultimately murdered for is that when violence asymmetries exist and one party holds itself to higher ethical standards than another party the more violent party can hold the less violent party's interests hostage and permanently ignored. If one party is willing to use tools such as hostage taking, blowing up civilian buses, concreting over the other party's holiest sites, threatening excavators of historical sites and ultimately using nuclear weapons to destroy a civilization that party can continue the delusion that the other's civilization is stunted and lacking legitimacy. Having Jews worship a golden Islamic shrine at their holiest site is the ultimate humiliation ritual. But it persists because of the violence asymmetry. If there was no asymmetry Jews would demand the same rights to control Islam's holiest site at Mecca as Muslims have at Judaism's holiest site at the Temple Mount and threaten to blow up worshippers at Mecca if those rights were withdrawn. Judeo-Christian ethics (rightly in my opinion) prevent Jews from threatening to blow up innocent civilian worshippers. But Islamic ethics seem not to. There is no respect for the rights of non Islamic civilizations and the history of those civilizations which generally outdate the Islamic civilizations. Like the actual genocidal dictators such as Hitler and Pol Pot, rather than those falsely accused of genocide in recent times, there seems to be a desire to restart from Year Zero and destroy what came before. Pol Pot and the Khmer Rouge attempted to erase Cambodian history, remove all vestiges of the past including the "corruption" of Western capitalist ideas and start afresh. The result from an actual genocide rather than a fake one was up to 2 million killed. Whilst Jews and Christians (again rightly in my opinion) preserve Islamic history including at the National Library of Israel which I recently visited, Muslims show a desire to erase and destroy Jewish and Christian history to make Islam Year Zero. These asymmetries make a paired civilization with Islam impossible.

"How dreadful are the curses which Mohammedanism lays on its votaries! Besides the fanatical frenzy, which is as dangerous in a man as hydrophobia in a dog, there is this fearful fatalistic apathy. The effects are apparent in many countries. Improvident habits, slovenly systems of agriculture, sluggish methods of commerce, and insecurity of property exist wherever the followers of the Prophet rule or live.... The fact that in Mohammedan law every woman must belong to some man as his absolute property - either as a child, a wife, a concubine - must delay the final extinction of slavery until the faith of Islam has ceased to be a great power among men.... No stronger retrograde force exists in the world.... were it not that Christianity is sheltered in the strong arms of science, the science against which it had vainly struggled, the civilisation of modern Europe might fall, as fell the civilisation of ancient Rome." Sir Winston Churchill (The River War)

Israel has been hardened in the past century against the notion that a Judeo-Islamic civilization can function and results in anything other the death, suffering and the attempted destruction of the Jewish population. Some, like Rabbi Meir Kahane and Itamar Ben-Gvir, knew all along. Others needed the terrorist attacks of October 7th 2023 before they were able to come to this realization despite many living through the Second Intifada and civilian buses being blown up on an almost weekly basis. Rewarding this terrorism with land is almost as absurd as Jews worshipping a golden Islamic shrine at their holiest site. But even today Jews protest to reward the October 7th hostage takers with favorable negotiation terms so the hostage takers can regroup, rearm and repeat. A significant minority of the native population will, no matter what happens and how dreadful the circumstances, remain so absurdly stupid and shortsighted that nation states can't afford to pair them with a significant Muslim minority to take advantage of them. The native population, however stupid, can't be removed but the size of the Muslim minority can be managed downwards. Unfortunately the rest of the West has not been hardened like Israel has. It is on a trajectory to learn in the most painful fashion imaginable that a Christian-Islamic civilization will not turn out any better than an attempted Judeo-Islamic one. Although the predominantly Pakistani grooming gangs in the UK might seem like a nadir (what can be worse than your kids being sexually abused whilst the police force and state protects the perpetuators?) this is only the start without the mother of all 180 degree u-turns. And whilst all organs of the state and the King of England welcome Islam in as the new national religion and imprison those who protest it there is no peaceful path to course correct.

## 72 When all roads lead to Baruch Goldstein portraits on the wall

In 1994 Baruch Goldstein entered a mosque in the Cave of the Patriarchs in Hebron and opened fire killing 29 and wounding 125 Muslim worshippers. It was an extremely rare example of a Jewish terrorist attack and Jews no longer standing for the blatant violence asymmetry amongst wave after wave of Islamic terrorism. Until recently Ben-Gvir hung a portrait of Goldstein at his home as a symbol that when pushed to extremes Jews were also capable of carrying out the same evil acts that Arabs were capable of. The entire purpose of democratic systems, other than as a mechanism for the peaceful transfer of power, is to provide the electorate with the ability to vote for legislative agendas that resolve the problems and the challenges they are facing. During the First and Second Intifadas there was nothing more pressing than putting a stop to Jewish civilians being repeatedly blown up in suicide bombings. The Israeli democratic system was unable to do that and all it could come up with is to offer the terrorists land in exchange for peace and banning those like Rabbi Meir Kahane who suggested that Arab deportations were the only answer. I personally do not condone Goldstein's actions. However, good people being forced to do evil things to match the evil that evil people are capable of is a story as old as time. Do I condone the dropping of nuclear bombs on Hiroshima and Nagasaki? Do I condone the carpet bombing of Dresden by Allied forces in 1945? When all else fails, war is the only option and only one side can win absolutely nothing can be off the table. Once you've got to that point all systems have failed. It is the responsibility of those with power and influence within those systems to offer release valves and paths to course correct so that future Baruch Goldsteins don't think the only option left available to them is resorting to the same evil that is being perpetuated on their people. In a way I'm disappointed Ben-Gvir took the portrait down. As Minister of National Security he now has the ability within the democratic system to deliver on ensuring intifadas and October 7ths never happen to the Jewish people within Israel again. If he fails to do that I can't think of a better cautionary tale than the eyes of Baruch Goldstein looking down on him at the breakfast table.

It is July 27th 2025 and coming up to two years since the October 7th terrorist attacks and all sides seem to be conspiring to ensure the worst case scenario occurs in Gaza. An endless war where young Israeli soldiers continue to die for seemingly no reason with unclear military objectives, a global propaganda war that Israel is losing as Gazans struggle to gain access to food and medical supplies, Israeli hostages that remain in captivity with no timetable on attempting to free them by force and ending a near two year negotiation process with terrorists; in short it is a total mess and the speculative excuses for a seeming total lack of leadership are running extremely bare. During the era of US Presidents pushing foolhardy, idiotic and unrealistic two state solutions Netanyahu's prevarication and evasion was a major asset. Today with a sympathetic US President his inability to lay out a clear strategy for ending the war in Gaza is killing Israeli soldiers, starving Gazans and driving Israel's global reputation into the mud. For every Israeli soldier that dies in Gaza that soldier's family should ask what they died for and hold Netanyahu responsible. It is becoming absolutely pathetic. How long is Israel going to negotiate with terrorists? It is already coming up to 2 years. Another year? Another 5 years? Another 10? What is going to happen to the approximately 2 million Gaza inhabitants? Is Gaza going to be rebuilt with those 2 million still there reverting back to the situation on October 6th? Are they going to be killed by bombings or mass starvation? Or are those who don't want to fight a war going to be moved to an alternative territory in the Arab world or in Africa? Netanyahu repeatedly goes to the White House bearing souvenirs and Nobel Peace Prize nominations like a souvenir salesman whilst Israelis and Gazans die due to his inability to formulate a strategy for ending the war. It is true that many Gazans supported Hamas and celebrated in the aftermath of the October 7th terrorist attacks, perhaps even a majority. But if they're out of Gaza many miles from Israel does it really matter? Would you prefer to kill 2 million people either quickly by bombing or slowly by mass starvation? It is true that Egypt and other Arab nation states are determined to keep those 2 million Gazans trapped in a warzone and have done for decades but Africa and the world is a big place. Is there really no territory on the planet that will take them in exchange for cash? Netanyahu has no answers to any of these questions and his lack of leadership is ensuring everyone loses. But sure, keep popping over to America with a new souvenir under your arm as Israelis and Gazans continue to die with no end in sight.

Ben-Gvir and Smotrich are in a difficult position. Understandably they don't want to trash Netanyahu's legacy. I'm sure they believe (as I do) that without Netanyahu who knows how much weaker a position Israel would be in today both militarily and economically? In addition, in a multitude of ways they owe their political careers to Netanyahu. The Overton window has shifted rightwards under Netanyahu's leadership and positions on a whole range of issues that were considered fringe earlier in Netanyahu's career are now considered universal wisdom within Israel. He has created the space for Ben-Gvir and Smotrich to take positions of responsibility in a coalition government when previously figures like Kahane struggled to even maintain a seat in the Knesset. However, despite all that, at some point a tough choice rears its head. Are you capable of succeeding him and advancing your own positions that might conflict with Netanyahu's traveling souvenir salesman approach or will you get dragged down with the ship? Ben-Gvir and Smotrich may feel like that time is not yet here and they need to continue to expand their electoral popularity remaining under Netanyahu's wing. There may be a broader long term military strategy in play and intelligence that I'm not aware of. But post the attacks on the Iranian nuclear sites and wars with Iranian proxies in Lebanon and elsewhere what exactly could that longer term strategy be and is it dependent on Netanyahu remaining leader? Elections have to be held in Israel by the end of 2026. Is that the time to go for broke or should they wait another election cycle? On a whole range of issues I personally believe Ben-Gvir and Smotrich present the most positive vision for a stronger Israel post October 7th rather than returning to October 6th weakness and being under the thumb of terrorists. But how to get there with a Israel's longest serving leader shaped obstacle in the way? 

I suspect the majority of the Israeli electorate and even the families of the fallen soldiers would accept casualties destroying Iran's nuclear capabilities or removing Hamas' ability to fire rockets into the Israeli mainland as the unfortunate but necessary cost of military action. Similarly I suspect they would accept casualties in a successful or failed attempt to save hostages who have been held in captivity in Gaza for approaching two years, just as Netanyahu had to come to terms with the death of his brother attempting to save hostages from Entebbe in 1976. Sending soldiers into the Gazan meat grinder to die with no obvious military objectives and no plan for removing the 2 million Gazan inhabitants to ensure a peaceful post October 7th world is however unacceptable. If Netanyahu considers it inevitable that those 2 million Gazans remain indefinitely and considers it inevitable that Gaza returns back to its October 6th state then Netanyahu might as well just admit his official policy is Gaza disengagement part 2 and stop with the façade that is killing Israeli soldiers for no reason. There is no peaceful end state where somehow Hamas is eradicated but those 2 million Gazans remain. It is impossible to identify where future Hamas fighters end and innocent Gazan civilians begin. But without a plan to remove them Netanyahu is just delaying the inevitable. Prevarication and evasiveness achieve nothing. Those who consider themselves innocent civilians need to be relocated and those who consider themselves Hamas fighters can choose to stay and fight a war they will lose. Those in the international community who want to whine about this being "ethnic cleansing" can justify why they were willing to keep 2 million Gazans trapped in a warzone for 2 years. And explain why in a supposed "genocide" there are still 2 million Gazans around to relocate. I personally much prefer the relocation option to the Hiroshima or Dresden option and think all options for relocation need to be explored and ruled out before the Hiroshima or Dresden option are even considered. But there will be a hell of a lot of blame to go round if those worst case scenarios end up occurring and top of the blame list will be Egypt for keeping Gazans trapped in a warzone and the Arab world for refusing to accept fellow Arab refugees into their countries to escape war.

## 73 The Temple Within

"We must remember that the details of the Temple are a model for and reflection of the inner structure of the human soul. For this reason, rebuilding the Temple is integral to and a manifestation of Redemption. It indicates the completion of our Divine mission, transforming the world into a dwelling place for G\*dliness. Obviously, then, we must not only understand the mystical relationship between the external Temple and our internal soul, but we must internalize the Divine service. We must translate the Temple's vessels and activities into our own. Rebuilding our inner Temple, our inner Holy Temple, is the first step toward rebuilding the Temple in Jerusalem." Dovid Yisroel Ber Kaufman (based on the talks of the Lubavitcher Rebbe)

You should expect the enemy to say or do anything to defeat you, paralyze you or stunt your growth. The enemy is not doing their job effectively if they don't do everything in their power to achieve this. Sometimes it isn't clear whether a particular person or group of people is hovering around neutrality or is indeed a direct enemy. When it comes to the multitude of Arab nation states that surround Israel it sometimes isn't clear where they sit on this spectrum between neutrality and direct enemy. Iran has obviously been a direct enemy of Israel since the Islamic revolution in 1979. But Qatar? Saudi Arabia? They are supposedly allies of the United States (Qatar provided President Trump with a 400 million dollar luxury jetliner to be used as Air Force One for example) and the United States is Israel's most significant ally. By that logic surely Qatar and Saudi Arabia don't veer too far away from neutrality right? It depends on what you think Israel and Judaism should be. If you think Israel should be locked in an infinite war with a non-existent state with uncertain borders and have its strength and vitality permanently sapped by this infinite war then you could certainly argue that Qatar and Saudi Arabia are no worse than neutral. If you think Jews should never have sovereignty over their holiest site and to the extent that they are allowed up there at all they should worship in the direction of a golden Islamic shrine you could certainly argue that Qatar and Saudi Arabia are no worse than neutral. However, if you think Israel and Judaism should aim for more than this pitiful existence then the further you move away from those positions the more Qatar and Saudi Arabia start to look like direct enemies. This is why I think pursuing expansion of the Abraham Accords is a double edged sword and ultimately a waste of time. Declaring sovereignty over land in Gaza, Judea, Samaria and the Temple Mount and announcing your intention to start the rebuilding of the Third Temple only needs to happen once. Arab nation states in the Abraham Accords will never agree to it and so attempting to do this within the confines of the Abraham Accords seems like a recipe for a neverending pitiful existence status quo. But they're Arab nation states. You can't really expect them to be any better than neutral actors even in the best case scenario. There is a significant subset (if not a majority) of Arabs and Muslims in every Arab nation state that see the mere existence of Israel as an affront to their religious beliefs. In many cases they have been encouraged to believe this by their own leaders. That is not where the challenge or the opportunity lies. If fellow Jews can't be convinced that Israel and Judaism should aim for more than a pitiful existence it really doesn't matter what the direct enemies or quasi neutral observers think. A pitiful existence it shall remain.

Israel's political and religious leaders need to offer more. I'm not convinced that if Netanyahu was in power for another 50 years that he'd ever seek to change the status quo on the Temple Mount. Everything and anything would be perceived as more pressing and less worthy of expending political capital on either domestically or internationally. Ben-Gvir is the one who has pushed and continues to push the envelope on the Temple Mount. Even today on Tisha B'Av 2025, the day when Jews fast and commemorate the destruction of the first two temples, Ben-Gvir was breaking new ground as the first ever minister to lead prayers on Judaism's holiest site. Too many of Israel's secular political leaders today still see the Temple Mount as Moshe Dayan did in the aftermath of the Six Day War when he reportedly asked "What do I need all this Vatican for?" (Jerold Auerbach, JNS.org, "A tragic Israeli surrender"). Too many of Israel's religious leaders still subscribe to the view that Jews are helpless observers to fate and have no role to play in making Judaism's holiest site relevant again let alone restored to previous grandeur. It is this both unholy and holy alliance within Israel allied with the direct enemies and quasi neutral observers in the Arab world that will seek to ensure generation after generation are entirely dependent on the emergence of the Jewish Moshiach or a miracle from G\*d to save them. G\*d is capable of making things happen but G\*d is also capable of stopping things from happening. It is the height of complacency and pomposity to demand human inaction in the face of clear injustices and inferior outcomes because somehow that is what G\*d wants from you. Since when did "Leave everything for Moshiach to complete and stay exclusively at home reading books" become such an influential strand of Judaism?

"Through the studying about the Temple, on some level the Temple exists. And when we study about the Temple, it's as if we are building the Temple... that particularly when we can't see the Temple, it's so important, so significant to study about it, because that in fact builds the Temple. Perhaps it could be compared to an architect. Prior to building a building, you need to have drawings. One needs to go to engineers to get the papers done. And when studying about it and drawing it on the papers, it's actually as if you're building it. Building doesn't begin when the hammer hits the nail or when the wood delivery or stone delivery is made. So studying about the Temple is equivalent and brings about the building of the Temple on some level. In addition to that, studying about the Temple also causes a yearning. It's hard to yearn for something when you don't know what it is that you're yearning for. So when we study about the Temple, it enables us to properly desire and yearn for the rebuilding of the Holy Temple, the Third Holy Temple." Rabbi Levi Jacobson (chabad.org course on Inside G\*d's Home: The Holy Temple)

G\*d granted humans agency and generally the freedom to choose how they spend their time on this planet. Study is critically important. Without study one may never fully understand or appreciate wisdom from the divine or from ancient sages and one certainly can't build constructions in the world of atoms, world of bits or the world of the divine without study. But without application or at least circulation of that wisdom what you learn is wasted. It goes to the grave with you. This is what is so frustrating about so much of the religious leadership within Israel and certainly the modern day leadership of the Haredi in the Knesset. They want all the benefits of living in the modern day nation state of Israel with none of the responsibilities. They want endless financial handouts, universal exclusions from army service and to be put on a pedestal by the rest of the Israeli electorate without giving anything back. The leader of the Shas party, Aryeh Deri, was convicted of taking 155,000 dollars in bribes in 1999 and spent 3 years in prison so it is perhaps not a surprise that his prime focus since returning to politics has been taking secular, left wing positions, maximizing state handouts for his party's supporters and avoiding any responsibilites to contribute to the state. Deri has even discussed cooperation with secular left wing leaders to prevent Ben-Gvir and other Jews from visiting the Temple Mount (Times of Israel, August 2024). If the Haredi population was to remain a small minority then one could turn a blind eye to such weak and possibly corrupt leadership. However, with an average of seven children per family the Haredi population is projected to reach a third of the Israeli population by 2050 (Jerusalem Post, November 2021). Giving a third of the population military service exemptions and state handouts is not in any way sustainable not that Deri and the current Haredi leadership in the Knesset care. On nearly every political position they seem to take the opposite position to what "The Rebbe" advocated for, himself a Haredi rabbi (Hasidic). I don't know how this gets resolved or corrected but it is a significant and growing problem. It may need a higher quality of Haredi leader to make aliyah from abroad and dislodge the weak Haredi leadership within Israel. Whilst inspiring individuals like "The Rebbe" and Rabbi Levi Jacobson, who has put together an exceptional online course on "Inside G\*d's Home: The Holy Temple" on chabad.org, refuse to make aliyah to attempt to change Israel from within one hopes some viable alternatives can be found from within Israel.

"The fact that Adam was created from there, the fact that the world was created from there, this is where it all started. This is where the energy, the power and the strength, the glory of G\*d was experienced and seen, where Hashem expressed Himself most. And this is the natural place for Hashem to be seen and experienced once again. Look at the Beit Hamikdash as the soul is for the body, the Beit Hamikdash, the Holy Temple, is for the world." Rabbi Levi Jacobson

If the site of the Beit Hamikdash is as the soul is for the body then the soul in its current form has been almost entirely destroyed. There are the remains of a wall to remind oneself of where it used to be but nothing more. There is a single gate to access it from but your spiritual leaders forbid you from entering it. The soul must be controlled by Muslims and Muslims can tread over and sully the holiest parts of it with no repercussions. The few in public life who don't want to accept this reality and agitate for change and progress are demonized by their own soulless Jewish media. The soul of Judaism must be exclusively a place for suffering and regret for what happened thousands of years ago until a single Jew appears claiming to be the Jewish Moshiach. Until then Jews must stay at home, helpless, to work towards a brighter tomorrow and a plausible roadmap for the soul being restored its previous glory and grandeur. This cannot be Judaism. If it is it really should have died out millennia ago.

## 74 When the old man can't pull the trigger

"Perhaps we are all Aladdins, every novel idea is a kind of magic lamp able to bring forth the creative spirit... till it becomes obsolete. Perhaps herein lies the real achievement of victory when the victor becomes dispensable." Ze'ev Jabotinsky

The carcass of the two state solution still wriggling and lashing out lays before him. A mountain of Jewish (and Arab) corpses lies in its wake after decades of carnage. "It can still be revived. Its quality of life will be diminished but we can't live without it" Naftali Bennett insists. Arabs and Europeans in the pocket of the Arabs shriek from the sidelines "There will never be peace unless you keep this animal alive". President Trump looks over at him bemused "Isn't this what you worked your whole life for? This moment? I spent my first term thinking you were willing to pursue a two state solution. But you weren't. You won Bibi." Ben-Gvir takes a gun out of his holster and passes it to him. "It is only right you do this. You deserve this moment" he whispers in his ear. Netanyahu looks over at the Attorney General. "The Attorney General won't let me do it" he says. Ben-Gvir shakes his head. "The Supreme Court will put me in prison for years for accepting champagne as a gift" he says. Ben-Gvir shakes his head. "The Abraham Accords will fall apart if I do this" he says. Ben-Gvir shakes his head. "The UN...." Ben-Gvir shakes his head. "It can be given a pen and food. It won't pose a threat anymore. It won't do anymore harm. Regardless it isn't the right time. There are more intermediate steps that need to be followed before..." Ben-Gvir shakes his head and motions towards the gun. Netanyahu holds the gun up tentatively in the direction of the wriggling carcass. The Arab and European shrieking gets louder and louder. Netanyahu shakes his head and places the gun on the table. "It's not the right time" he insists. Ben-Gvir shrugs his shoulders. "So be it. Leave it to me Bibi" he sighs as he places his hand on his shoulder.

There is no halfway house despite Netanyahu constantly flailing for one. Either Gaza, Judea and Samaria are part of Israeli sovereign territory or they are placeholders for new, different nation state(s). After all the devastation and loss of life in Gaza it is insane to rebuild a placeholder for a new, different nation state controlled and governed by Arabs who can choose to pass it off to the Palestinian Authority or Hamas mark 2 at the time of their choosing. Absolutely insane. But if it isn't going to be Israeli sovereign territory that is the only intellectually honest alternative. It sounds harsh but if the Israeli electorate can't be convinced that it is a straight choice between sovereignty and reverting back to October 6th insanity then they don't deserve a viable nation state. They will deserve decades more of border uncertainty, intifadas and October 7ths. Stupidity, especially in the Middle East, is lethal. But it isn't just Israel and Gazans that are suffering through Netanyahu's flailing. There has never been and perhaps never will be again an American administration that is this supportive of Israel emerging from its "two state solution" nightmare once and for all. The longer the situation drags on and the more Netanyahu drags his heels the more images and news stories come out of Gaza that can be used to demonize Israel and Israel's allies. Trump and the Republicans cannot afford to continue to be dragged down by this constant barrage of "genocide" propaganda especially when Israel is not the sole American foreign policy priority and when there is a domestic policy agenda that is arguably the most challenging for almost a century. The situation is even more absurd given the Knesset and Netanyahu's own political party (Likud) voted to apply sovereignty in Judea and Samaria in July 2025. So that only leaves Gaza. A two state solution with Gaza as the second state? Or Israeli sovereignty over Gaza? It is your land or it isn't. It is part of Israel or it isn't. It is your responsibility or it isn't. You want more October 7ths or you don't. It really is that simple. I can only assume we are witnessing the results of age and being in power too long. There is no way a younger Netanyahu would look a gift horse in the mouth like this and desperately scramble round for any alternative other than the most obvious option and the only option that hasn't yet been tried. Sovereignty. Finality. Pull the damn trigger.

## 75 Designating space for the world of the divine

It requires strenuous and sustained effort to firstly carve out space in the world of atoms and world of bits for the world of the divine and then defend and preserve that space. Unlike the world of atoms and world of bits that in the modern world especially will frame and envelop your existence at all times (how many times per day does one think about collecting more money or Instagram notifications?) the world of the divine can only be experienced when you've expended the effort to create a space for it to enter. You can see this effort expended by Jews scurrying around the Jerusalem markets in the hours preceding the Jewish Sabbath (Shabbat) before everything closes down at nightfall. This is an example of creating and preserving space in the calendar or the time dimension for the world of the divine. This seems to come naturally to many modern day Jews. The Hebrew essayist Ahad Ha'am famously stated that in exile from their land "More than Jews have kept Shabbat, Shabbat has kept the Jews". When it comes to defending and preserving space in the world of atoms on Temple Mount it seems to come less naturally. This is perhaps to be expected. Whilst Jews (generally) had access to and control of their time in exile it is a relatively new phenomenon to have the ability to access and control their holiest site. Many seem to not know what to do this newfound ability and would rather keep their heads in the sand, pretend they are still in exile and follow the advice of their ancestors who were never granted this ability. And yet the site of the Temple Mount sits there, accessible to Jews in a land that is once again (nominally at least) controlled by Jews. This week "There is a Holocaust in Gaza" graffiti in Hebrew was sprayed on the Western Wall reportedly by a young Haredi man (Times of Israel, August 11th 2025). It was admittedly a single man's actions and a sample size of one. However, it is emblematic of the problems created by leaving vacuums for foreign religions and ideologies to fill rather than defending and preserving spaces for the world of the divine. A vacuum in the mind of this self hating young Haredi man, a vacuum on what is supposedly the holiest site for Judaism and a vacuum in Gaza where inaction and indecisiveness increasingly leads to demonization from within and from afar. In Jerusalem and all over the world Jews lead the world in designating space for the world of the divine in the time dimension. But in the world of atoms and the world of the bits they are failing miserably. If you can't achieve it on your holiest site where can you achieve it?

It is the year 2100 CE or the Hebrew year 5860. A father takes his young son to the Western Wall in the Old City of Jerusalem for the first time. "Today we are going to the holiest and most sacred place in the world", the father tells him. "The whole world?", the son asks inquisitively. "Yeah the whole world. This is where Hashem himself chooses to dwell." "Whoa. Why did Hashem choose here? Is it the best place? Is it better than Disneyland?" The father smiles, "For Hashem it is. Disneyland is fun for kids but this is Hashem's favorite place." They arrive within sight of the Western Wall and the father points towards the wall. "There it is", he says. "I can't see anything", the son says confused, "There's just a wall. What's behind the wall?" "We can't go behind the wall. That's where Hashem dwells", the father answers. "No one is allowed past the wall?", the son asks. "Some people are. Muslims are. Our rabbi forbids us." The son scrunches up his face. "Hashem allows the Muslims past the wall to get closer to him? But he doesn't want us Jews to get closer to him?". The father looks at his son sympathetically. "It is not like that son. We just have to wait for Moshiach and the Temple to be rebuilt." "What are the Muslims doing behind the wall? Are they going to rebuild the Temple for Moshiach?" The father sighs, "I don't know. Only Hashem knows." The son looks up at his father bemused and then at the wall. "Is Hashem punishing us?" The father shrugs his shoulders, "I don't know son. Let's go closer to the wall and pray for Moshiach." On the journey home the son looks at his father "I think Hashem should move to Disneyland. He'd have more fun there." The father smiles wryly, "Perhaps you're right son". They drive past a newspaper stand with the headline "Day 28,079 of the war: IDF bombs Gaza, 35 dead". A stand next to the newspaper stand is selling spray paint canisters on special offer.

It is the year 2100 CE or the Hebrew year 5860. A father takes his young son to the Western Wall in the Old City of Jerusalem for the first time. "Today we are going to the holiest and most sacred place in the world", the father tells him. "The whole world?", the son asks inquisitively. "Yeah the whole world. This is where Hashem himself chooses to dwell." "Whoa. Why did Hashem choose here? Is it the best place? Is it better than Disneyland?" The father smiles, "You'll see. Look out the window. Mount Moriah should be coming into view soon." Sure enough as they turn the corner a stone structure built on top of Mount Moriah towering over all of Jerusalem comes into view. The father looks over at his son with his eyes glued out of the window as the car pulls into a parking space by a mikvah (ritual bath, מקוה) on the outskirts of Jerusalem, "C'mon. Let's prepare ourselves for Hashem".

## 76 A trip to the National Library

"I had found my religion: nothing seemed more important to me than a book. I saw the library as a temple." Jean-Paul Sartre

A week earlier the father had taken his son to the National Library in Jerusalem to see the "Rebuilding the Beit Hamikdash" exhibition. As they reached the entrance the father pointed out the stone exterior of the building, "Look how the stones have gaps in. The builders made it look like the Western Wall which we're going to next week. The light of Hashem shines through the cracks." They went through security and down the stairs to the exhibition. The first section documented the efforts of various Jews to keep the dream of rebuilding the Beit Hamikdash alive during the close to two millennia of exile. Chief among them was Maimonides ("The Rambam") who outlined the specifications for rebuilding the Holy Temple in exhaustive detail in his Mishneh Torah back in the 12th century CE. "Why did it take so long to build?", the son asked, "Did the Rambam think it would take a thousand years?" The father again smiled, "I don't think so. I think he would have been very sad to hear it would take a thousand years. But he did his part. He couldn't have done any more. I'm sure he's happy you are still asking about him after all this time." The second section focused on the reclaiming of the Temple Mount from one IDF paratrooper raising the Israeli flag on it during the Six Day War to another IDF paratrooper, Rabbi Yisrael Ariel, founding the Temple Institute and serving under Rabbi Meir Kahane in the Kach party to the Kach activist rising to the office of Prime Minister and declaring the end of the Islamic Waqf administration on the Temple Mount and full Jewish rights many decades after the initial flag raising. "I don't understand", the son said confused, "We won the Temple Mount in the Six Day War. Why did the Muslims control it after that?" "It seems to be the Jewish way", the father responded, "We turn military victories into political defeats. The soldiers act like lions and the politicians act like sheep. We have to try all the wrong options before we settle on the right one. Before Ben-Gvir became Prime Minister the Jewish media hated him for daring to pray on the Temple Mount as a Jew. Rabbi Meir Kahane was banned from the Knesset. Rabbi Yisrael Ariel was arrested for bowing down on the Temple Mount. We Jews are our own worst enemy. We are capable of sinning and turning away from Hashem just like everybody else. Thankfully Hashem never gave up on us despite it all." "If I was Hashem I would have given up", the son said indignantly. The father smiled, "One day you'll have a son. And he will do stupid things and rebel against you and rebel against Hashem. But you won't give up on him whatever he does. One day you'll rebel against me. But while I'm here I won't give up on you. And Hashem will never give up on you. C'mon let's move on to the next section. This is the fun part. This is where we rebuild the Beit Hamikdash."

"The Rebbe Reb Elimelech dreamed that the Third Temple was being rebuilt. And he saw millions of people -- or maybe they were angels -- running around, working like crazy. So he stopped one of the angels and said "You are wasting so much time. If you had fewer people who wouldn't fall all over each other, you could be finished so much faster." The angel laughed at him and said, "You don't understand, Reb Elimelech. G\*d wants as many people as possible to have a part in the rebuilding of the Beit Hamikdash..." Teachings of Rabbi Shlomo Carlebach (The Soul of Jerusalem)

The next section of the exhibition focused on the actual rebuilding from the ceremony for the first stone laid to the evolution of the architectural plans and the miniature scale models housed at the Israel Museum round the corner from the National Library. The father led his son to a computerized touchscreen. "Can you type your surname in?", he asked. With some assistance the son pressed the Hebrew letters of his surname before pressing enter. "Do you recognize him?", the father asked with a pause, "It is your grandfather". "Whoa", the son exclaimed, "What is saba (סבא) doing here?" "He laid a stone in the rebuilding of the Holy Temple", the father responded as he navigated from the photo to the page displaying the location of the stone that the grandfather had laid. The user interface and database search functionality had been reused with minor modifications from the Central Database of Shoah Victims' Names at Yad Vashem, the Holocaust Remembrance Center on Mount Herzl. Jewish visitors to Jerusalem could now go from looking up their ancestors' involvement in the Holocaust at Yad Vashem to looking up their more recent ancestors' involvement in the rebuilding of the Holy Temple. "Next week we'll try to find the exact location of the stone your grandfather laid", the father told the son, "He'd have wanted you to see it". On the way out of the exhibition something caught the son's eye in the National Library shop. He pointed to it and asked expectantly, "Can we get it? I want to be like saba." The father looked up. It was a do-it-yourself craft kit for building a model of the Holy Temple.

The father watched his son play with his toys. The days were passing and dust was gathering on the unopened do-it-yourself craft kit on the shelf. The father was anxious that his son assemble it before their visit to the Holy Temple but didn't want to apply any pressure or even persuasion to do so. He wanted his son to associate the activity with a continuance of self directed play under free will rather than imposing his own will on his son's playtime activities and the son blindly following instructions by rote. But at the same time he didn't know how crowded it would be on their upcoming visit and how many of the inner sanctums of the Holy Temple they would be able to see. If the son was familiar with the general layout prior to the visit it wouldn't matter too much. He would at least have a mental model of the entire area and a frame of reference for the parts that were accessible and viewable to general visitors. Hopefully this would sustain the son's interest on the day rather than trudging around crowded areas feeling like a chore. But the son continued playing with his toys oblivious to the restless machinations in his father's mind. And the clock on the wall kept ticking closer and closer to their scheduled visit. The mother walked in. "What's this?", she asked, holding up the unopened craft kit. "It's the Beit Hamikdash", the son answered, "I'm going to build it like saba." "You're going to build it? Wow. I hope it doesn't take you as long as it took to build the actual one. Want to start now?" The son nodded and the mother opened up the packaging. 
## 77 Assembling the Holy Temple

"If Jews cannot get to the holy places, the holy places will come to them." Hans Kroch

In 1962 (Hebrew year 5722) Hans Kroch, the builder and owner of the Holyland Hotel in Jerusalem, approached Michael Avi-Yonah, professor of Archaeology at the Hebrew University, with a proposal to build an ambitiously sized model of Second Temple Jerusalem at a scale of 1:50 (2 centimeters representing a life-sized meter). Kroch wanted to dedicate it to the memory of his son Jacob who had fell in the 1948 War of Independence defending his kibbutz (Nitzanim) against Egyptian attack. At the time of the proposal, five years before the Six Day War, Jordan controlled East Jerusalem, the Old City and the Temple Mount and Jews were blocked from accessing them by thick concrete walls. A year after the model was completed and opened to the public the Six Day War was fought, the walls came down and Jews could once again walk freely around the entirety of Jerusalem as if they were Lego minifigures in Kroch's model. The model took four years to build and consisted of over five million tiny stone blocks with the Holy Temple and its courts requiring 650 columns molded in fiberglass and covered with gold leaf (Model of Jerusalem in the Second Temple Period, David Amit). It was assembled according to the prevailing understanding of Second Temple Jerusalem but after the model was completed and the Six Day War opened Jerusalem up to archaeological excavations more and more sections of the model were found to be historically inaccurate. A feedback loop developed where archaelogists would study parts of the model, carry out excavations at those sites, make new discoveries and submit proposals to Avi-Yonah to update his model. Although the cost of making changes to his model was prohibitive and interpretations of new discoveries often conflicted Avi-Yonah and his successors did make changes when the interpretations were proved beyond reasonable doubt and the passage of time did not throw up any more counterfactuals. Indeed before his death in 1974 (Hebrew year 5734) he began the redesign of the area to the south of the Temple Mount after some consequential discoveries were made in one particular excavation. Avi-Yonah was not rigidly protective of the veracity of his model, was transparent about which areas of it were more speculative, stayed true to the spirit of the scientific process and unlike broad swathes of the Islamic world and a subset of Jewish rabbis welcomed the pursuit towards a greater human understanding of Judaism's holiest sites.

The Israel Museum opened in 1965 (Hebrew year 5725) adjacent to the sites of the Knesset (opened in 1966), Supreme Court (opened in 1992) and the National Library (newest building opened in 2023). This was too late to be considered for the original site of Kroch's model, it was initially assembled on the grounds of Kroch's Holyland Hotel, but when an alternative site was sought away from planned developments the spacious 20 acre grounds of the Israel Museum were considered most suitable. The relaxed spatial constraints of the new site allowed for sculpting of the terrain to more closely resemble the landscape of the original city with valleys binding it on the east, south and west. Once this was completed attention turned to the transferring of the actual model requiring it to be chiseled into around 1,000 sections, transported and reassembled on top of the relevant contours. It reopened to public visitors at its permanent home within the grounds of the Israel Museum in 2006 (Hebrew year 5766). When thinking ahead to the building of Third Temple Jerusalem this exercise provides a template for thinking about the role of models, the deconstruction, transportation and possible reassembly at alternative sites of Islamic monuments such as the Dome of the Rock and the necessary preparation of the landscape on Temple Mount before the first stone can be laid. Although the transfer of Kroch's model required meticulous planning and delicate handling it wasn't overseen by the prominent rabbis and halakhic authorities of Israel's religious communities which clearly adds another dimension of complexity and a myriad of divergent views to an already fractious task. However, Kroch in collaboration with Avi-Yonah brought to life Second Temple Jerusalem and fulfilled the Torah commandment to build a Temple, if only a small one, adjacent to the land that Second Temple Jerusalem once stood. This is the first step to transitioning from paper to reality, from the exiled "people of the book" to the returned people of builders on their own land and ultimately bringing the world of atoms back into the world of the divine.

"When it comes to laying the foundation of a building, it is of no concern what neighbors or passersby might think of the outer attractiveness of the foundation, much less what scoffers might say about it. What is important is that the foundation be of tested and durable material that can withstand any erosive elements, and that it should be strong enough to support the upper floors that will be added to it. The same is true of the foundations of Torah and mitzvot. There is no better test than actual experience, and our Jewish people have the wisdom and conviction of thousands of years of experience, ever since Matan Torah at Sinai, that it is adherence to the Torah and mitzvot in the daily life that have preserved our people - both collectively and individually - through all possible crises, and made us the Eternal People." The Lubavitcher Rebbe (letter from "The Rebbe" to a newlywed couple)

"So where do we start?", the mother asked her son, "What comes first?". The son's attention seemed to be captured by a golden Menorah, the gold plated Ark of the Covenant and a golden door. "We need strong foundations and a strong base" she told him, "We don't want the Beit Hamikdash to fall down." The son nodded. "We're lucky. Saba and his friends had to first remove a golden dome before they could start on the base. Moses had to stop Jews worshipping a golden calf. Saba had to stop Jews worshipping a golden dome the Muslims had put there. We seem to have a problem with gold. Open this up." She passed him the base to open up and extend. "What do you think?", the mother asked, "Do you think this base is strong enough to keep the Beit Hamikdash standing forever?" The son seemed unsure. "How big is the Beit Hamikdash?", he responded. "Good question. Pretty big. Hashem wants it to be seen from all across Jerusalem. Let's add a second base on top of this first one to make sure. Fold these flaps and put them in the slots of the first base."

## 78 Welcome to Israel. Welcome to the problem

On September 30th 2025, the day before Judaism's holiest day of the year (Yom Kippur) started and a week before the two year anniversary of the October 7th terrorist attacks, I received my Israeli identity card (Teudat Zehut, תעודת זהות). That date will henceforth be the date I made aliyah to Israel and became an Israeli citizen although I don't receive my Israeli passport for another three months. Having entered Israel in April 2025 for potentially the last attempt at obtaining Israeli citizenship and remaining for almost six months through Iranian missile bombardments (is President Trump's Twelve Day War branding sticking?) and the occasional terrorist attack I had finally received a piece of laminated card with an ID number and a photo of my face that gives me the right to stay (and work) in Israel indefinitely. After years of struggling unsuccessfully to convince various UK rabbis to give me the Proof of Judaism letter required to apply for Israeli citizenship and six years since entering Israel for the first time on an all expenses paid Birthright trip, a multiyear period in which I was hedging my bets during optimistic phases and downright writing off my chances during pessimistic phases, I had finally achieved the goal. Unlike those who successfully finalize the aliyah process abroad, take their Israeli taxpayer funded one-way aliyah flight and pose for photos with Israeli flags and slogan boards by the plane at Ben Gurion airport with a flight load of others also making aliyah or more dramatically the former American spy Jonathan Pollard who kissed the airport tarmac before being greeted by Prime Minister Netanyahu I received my identity card in a dingy basement office in Tel Aviv with two presumably government employees sitting behind a desk rearranging stacks of forms and documents. One passed over my identity card and said "Welcome to Israel". The other laughed and said "Welcome to the problem". It wasn't a joyful or climactic experience. But after ten years of wrestling with the American and Israeli visa and immigration systems I did not care in the slightest. Anything else would not have been on-brand for my life. If anything, having mentally prepared for another setback on the day my extended war visa was expiring and tensing my metaphorical stomach for yet another gut punch it was a relief when none came. On Yom Kippur an appropriately named Muslim individual by the name of "Jihad" (Al-Shamie) mowed down and stabbed Jewish worshippers outside a Manchester synagogue whilst on bail for a suspected rape and the UK media was quick to blame mental illness, the "far right" stoking animosity and/or Israel's wars for "Jihad"'s actions. Anything to avoid offending the UK's effective owners and ruling classes wearing keffiyeh headscarves in the Middle East. If Israel is a "problem" I don't know what word you'd use to describe the UK in its current state. Welcome to the problem? As Marlo Stanfield would say in The Wire "Sound like one of dem good problems".

The first step recommended by the Jewish Agency post receiving the Israeli identity card is to open a Israeli bank account to amongst other things receive Sal Klita (סל קליטה, absorption basket) payments in shekels from the Ministry of Aliyah and Integration. These payments are intended to assist new immigrants with rental costs and Hebrew study within the first year of living in Israel. To receive these payments you obviously need to choose a bank and a branch. The largest banks in Israel are Bank Leumi and Bank Hapoalim who together, as of September 2022, hold a market share of approximately 60 percent when measured in terms of total system assets. As I write this in October 2025 Bank Leumi is valued (market capitalization) at approximately 92 billion shekels (28 billion US dollars) and Bank Hapoalim is valued at approximately 82 billion shekels (25 billion US dollars). When compared to the United States' largest bank, J.P. Morgan Chase (market capitalization of 800 billion US dollars), the United Kingdom's largest bank, HSBC (220 billion US dollars) and Australia's largest bank, Commonwealth Bank (183 billion US dollars) you can appreciate how small they are in a global context. This is at least partly explained by the population size of Israel (approximately 10 million people versus Australia's 27 million people) and Israel's relative youth (modern day nation state founded in 1948 versus Australia's 1901). Though other factors such as historical trade embargoes, being surrounded by generally hostile Arab nation states rather than relatively benign Asian nation states leading to a prioritization of other industries (e.g. defense) and perhaps global financial markets maturing before Israel's banking sector was able to get off the ground has led to a Israeli banking sector primarily focused on its small domestic market. With the Rothschild family historically playing such a pivotal role in obtaining the Balfour Declaration and funding the building of Israeli public institutions it is perhaps surprising that even in the investment banking realm the modern day Rothschild & Co. presence in Israel seems relatively limited. Does any of this matter? Should I randomly pick an Israeli retail bank, only use it when forced to pay or receive in shekels and instead continue to primarily use UK banking and Bitcoin services that charge less in fees? Is Israel's banking sector destined to always be small, domestic focused, unable to expand overseas, relatively bureaucratic and not a focus for growth or technological innovation? It does seem strange for a Jewish nation state with centuries of prominent Jewish bankers in the diaspora (Rothschild, Lehman Brothers, Goldman Sachs, Saloman Brothers etc) to relegate the financial sector to a sideshow. But then maybe that's a sector for American Jews and not Israeli Jews where the Israel stigma doesn't dampen the profits of companies founded and named after Jewish bankers.

I booked an appointment online to set up a bank account at Bank Hapoalim in Jerusalem. With my limited Hebrew taking photos of Hebrew text and uploading them to Google Translate for English translations is a technological g*dsend though many Israeli websites have English translations too. The Bank Hapoalim website is functional and perhaps no worse than the websites for some of the less technologically advanced incumbents I'm used to in the UK. With its small domestic market Israel doesn't seem to have experienced the challenger bank wave that the UK experienced in the 2010s with FinTech startups like Monzo, Revolut and Starling providing slick online and mobile experiences but with no physical branches and limited capacity to lend and issue mortgages. The in person bank account setup bureaucracy at Bank Hapoalim took a while, approximately 45 minutes, though the bank employee (Yisrael?) was very friendly and seemed pleasantly surprised there was a new immigrant opening a bank account with him. He asked what I did for work in broken English and I replied "Software, programming, computers" to which he responded "Ah, hi-tech" which sums up how banking isn't (yet) perceived as part of the technology (FinTech) sector in Israel. On completion of the paperwork he smiled and said "New bank account in Jerusalem. Baruch Hashem (ברוך השם, Blessed be G\*d)." Only in Israel. There's an interesting quirk with my name too that could be problematic with state bureaucracy in future. Michael (מיכאל) is fine, it is a Hebrew name that translates to "Who is like G\*d?" or "There is none like G\*d". But Folkson (פולקסון) has no Hebrew meaning and was spelt Fokson (פוקסון) without the "l" or "ל" (lamed) on my Israeli identity card. This is ironic because my Jewish ancestors changed their name from Falkson (with an "a") to Folkson (with an "o") when moving to the UK from modern day Latvia in the early 20th century. Do I keep my Hebrew surname as Fokson (פוקסון), put the "l" ("ל", lamed) back in, or change it to something else entirely? I don't have much time to decide, the Israeli state bureaucracy hasn't defeated me yet but it is asking for trouble if I let different spellings of my surname circulate on state documents and in state and banking computer systems. Still I have a bank account set up in a Jerusalem branch, it has a minimal amount of shekels in it and although the process certainly wasn't lightning fast it had a certain personal charm to it. Baruch Hashem indeed.

## 79 Israel's role in the global village

With the advent and propagation of the internet and social media platforms the world seemed to become smaller, more and more interconnected and increasingly resembled and was referred to as a "global village". The term was originally coined by Canadian media theorist Marshall McLuhan in the 1960s. As the world continues to shrink and American power over the internet and social media platforms cements itself to such an extent that the Americans can control information flow globally with impunity countries that don't accept their limited remit in this American controlled global village are going to come to a crossroads. One of the first countries to come to this crossroads will undoubtedly be Israel. The American remit for Israel is the effective church or synagogue of this global village engulfed in interminable conflicts with crazed jihadists to provide a sandbox for trying out the latest military technology in a perpetually hot environment. Unlike the mosque of this global village in Saudi Arabia, which must be protected from this chaos and bloodshed at all costs because that's where oil billionaires permanently live, the rich, powerful Americans can fly into visit the church or synagogue of this global village when there is a lull in hostilities and then fly back before they erupt again. There is a role for Israel in this global village but it is permanently dependent on the Americans for funding and donations, just like a church or synagogue is not able to independently financially sustain itself, and when the fighting gets too intense or the risk becomes too existential it leans on the Americans to ensure the church or synagogue of this global village doesn't get destroyed. The Americans won't let Israel be destroyed, the rich and powerful don't want the village church or synagogue to be destroyed, but they also don't want it straying into matters that a church or synagogue shouldn't concern itself. Money and power emanate from elsewhere in a partnership between the American billionaires and the Arab billionaires and the Chinese and Russian billionaires can be included in the partnership when their countries fulfill their global village remits. Wealthy American Jews may or may not want more for Israel than it has been given in its remit but given they don't plan to make permanent aliyah to Israel they would rather protect their wealth and power in the United States and not rock the boat. They can settle for the village synagogue not being destroyed, visiting during lulls in hostilities and sending some donations over to convince themselves they are being good Jews. What Israeli Jews will have to decide is whether they are willing to accept this remit in the global village going forward, especially as Israel's ceiling could be so much higher in a world where remits weren't allocated and actual capitalism, rather than faux olipolistic capitalism, was allowed to flourish.
