In theory Israel could emerge from post October 7th wars with relative stability on its borders, clear sovereignty over previously disputed lands in Gaza, Judea and Samaria (West Bank) and unleash a wave of human capital into a new iteration of startup nation. But in the global village that is not what the Americans and certainly not the Arabs want for Israel. The instability and uncertainty in Gaza, Judea and Samaria are by design. The global village church or synagogue can't get ideas above its station and return to innovating in fields that are now sewn up by American oligopolies if they are pemanently bogged down in 20 point peace plans and fretting about soldiers from nations that want Israel destroyed patrolling the streets of Gaza. All the living hostages may have returned from Gaza as I write this (baruch hashem) but after promising early signs and military successes, most impressively in Iran, the Trump administration is reverting to type and pursuing the same restraining of Israel foreign policy as a multitude of its predecessors. Gaza returning to its October 6th state now seems an inevitability via elaborate multi pointed peace plans and already wealthy Americans pandering to Arabs for yet more financial gain. And when Israel emerges from post October 7th wars (too premature to assume it is already) it may just find the world has become even smaller and its remit in the global village yet more constrained.

If the conflicts between Israel and Iran, Russia and Ukraine and China and Taiwan were all part of a 4-6 year world war like World War 1 and World War 2 there would be an argument to take American orders, keep the American oligopolies in place and make sure the American side won the war. But the introduction of nuclear weapons has changed the game. It is not clear how a world war would be won within 4-6 years without superpowers firing nuclear weapons at each other. Instead long, drawn out cold wars with semi-regular hot (not too hot) flare ups seems to be the inevitable long term future in the same vein as skirmishes between Oceania, Eurasia and Eastasia in George Orwell's 1984. In this scenario if you meekly take American orders for long cold war periods like a meek poodle it is not long before you turn into the UK of the 2025, teetering on national bankruptcy and failed state status. American interests are and never were perfectly aligned with British interests and the same is the case for the United States and Israel. Netanyahu has stood up for Israeli interests much better in the last two decades than any British leader since Thatcher but no Israeli leader can afford to take their foot off the gas. If there isn't what appears to be excessive friction between these supposed allies the Israeli leader isn't doing their job. Israel's story, 77 years in, is nowhere near finished even if the United States is just interested in maintaining its pre-eminent superpower status from the 20th century. You would hope Israel doesn't literally have to fight off American suffocation in a War of Independence like the Americans had to do with the British in the 18th century but American restraining of Israel is not going away. Meekly accepting failed vassal state status as the impoverished village church or synagogue seems to me to be the bigger risk. 

"When you look at the map of the Middle East Israel is a tiny little spot compared to these giant land masses. It's really a tiny spot. I actually said is there any way of getting more. It is so tiny." President Trump (August 2024)

"It is a small country in terms of land. See this pen, this wonderful pen. My desk is the Middle East and this pen, the top of the pen, is Israel. That's not good. It is a pretty big difference. I use that as an analogy. It's pretty accurate actually. It is a pretty small piece of land. It is amazing that they've been able to do what they've been able to do when you think about it. A lot of good, smart brainpower." President Trump (February 2025)

 "I'm not allowing Israel to annex the West Bank. There's been enough. It's time to stop now. Ok?" President Trump (September 2025)

"The policy of President Trump is that the West Bank will not be annexed. This will always be our policy." Vice President Vance (October 2025)

In the world of politics words often aren't worth the paper they are written on. Dominic Cummings described Boris Johnson as a "shopping trolley smashing between aisles" during Covid and with a 400 million dollar Qatari jet sitting in President Trump's shopping trolley from earlier in the year it isn't surprising that his trolley has since lurched in a pro Qatari position. Concerns over Israel's long term security and being too "tiny" evaporated pretty quickly. If sovereignty over Gaza, Judea and Samaria aren't the solution to Israel being too "tiny" what exactly is the solution? But then J.D. Vance is now the Vice President to the individual he previously described as "America's Hitler" so if you want some consistency get a dog? Perhaps becoming the von Papen to America's Hitler became too alluring a proposition. Assuming there isn't another shopping trolley swerve (and perhaps even if there is, what value is a Jekyll and Hyde ally?) a turning point has definitely been reached in US, Israeli relations. After struggling through four years of Biden's ramblings warning Israel not to pursue Hamas leader Sinwar in Rafah, southern Gaza the light at the end of the tunnel was a returning Trump and/or Republican adminstration that wanted a stronger, larger Israel and even introduced American legislation recognizing Judea and Samaria as land that Jews have legal and historic rights to and prohibiting the use of the term "West Bank" in US government documents (RECOGNIZING Judea and Samaria Act, 2025). Presumably deep in that legislation is a carve out for the President and the Vice President to do so. The previous hypothesis was that although Israel could no longer rely on Democrat administrations (Biden, Obama etc) in the United States it just had to wait for a Republican administration that under Trump had turned even more pro Israel than before. That hypothesis clearly no longer stands up to scrutiny. The frontrunners for Trump's successor at the time of writing, the Vice President and the Secretary of State (Marco Rubio), are fully signed up to this shopping trolley lurch. Netanyahu should not escape blame. When the American iron was hot and firing on pro Israel cylinders earlier in the year he didn't capitalize. Now it is cold and it is back to Netanyahu and Biden old men squabbling mode. The "Trump induced window of opportunity" I described earlier has passed and on Gaza, Judea and Samaria nothing has changed. Not only that but it looks like Netanyahu will be rewarded for doing nothing with another election win. You've gotta love politics.

## 80 Is Israel smart enough for where the world is headed?

"It [US abandoning Israel] would force Israel to seek new partners, likely including China... Israel is also on Beijing's shopping list. Push Israel away and China will welcome it. A Chinese-Israeli technological partnership would be a nightmare for America combining Israeli innovation with Chinese scale. America's alliance with Israel is not sentimental. It is strategic. While Israel benefits from American support, America benefits from Israel's considerable capabilities. In the Middle East no ally is stronger, more dependable or more aligned with American interest than Israel." Michael Doran, Is Israel a liability? (Prager University)

"We are certainly in the midst of a great transition to a multi-polar world, a post American order and a multi-polar world. No one can tell how the transition will unfold but there is no doubt it will be messy and unpredicatable because America is stepping back from its role as global insurer but there is no other country that's able to or willing to fill the vacuum. So we are in an uncomfortable position where the old rules do not apply anymore but the new ones have not been written. And we must brace ourselves for more turbulence ahead. So what are we to do in this environment? I think we cannot afford to just wait for things to happen or hope somehow that things magically will fall in place. We have to take actions now, plan now and start taking actions to invest together in tackling the problems of the global commons or in building new trade connections and keeping up the momentum of trade liberalisation. So that's something that Singapore is keen to do. We can't do it alone but we will do it with other like-minded countries." Lawrence Wong, Singapore Prime Minister (Financial Times interview, October 2025)

Every nation state has two faces: a front end that it presents to the domestic and international public and a back end that is generally private. The back end would encompass the intelligence services and the military to the extent that no nation state should want to leak critical military secrets to an adversary. When it comes to Israel's backend I have next to zero knowledge of how it operates but enough details bubble up to the public surface on successful operations such as the Stuxnet cyber attacks on Iranian nuclear facilities (2010), the pager supply chain attack on Hezbollah in Lebanon (2024) and the infiltration of Mossad cells deep inside Iran prior to the Twelve Day War (ok let's go with Trump's branding) in 2025 that the back end doesn't present a concern. One can never be complacent but at least as of 2025 it seems to be able to achieve things that require the highest levels of competence. The front end however really worries me. Everything is relative, Israel's front end is better than the UK's, a circus group of monkeys could offer a superior front end to the UK's and it is not clear that the UK's back end is much better than its front end. It is a relatively recent phenomenon in the West that the front end isn't treated seriously, it is effective entertainment and a reality TV show which Trump is perfect for after his lifetime of TV appearances including on "The Apprentice". In the UK Boris Johnson had a similar route to Brexit and the ascent to Prime Minister with regular appearances on TV series like "Have I Got News For You?". When I was younger I used to think this was a sign of strength, the Western peacock displaying its colorful feathers in complete contrast to a cold but highly competent back end. A message to the rest of the world that whilst leaders outside of the West boringly justified the results of their country's back ends the West could afford to put on an elaborate distracting show. Although generally considering itself part of the West, despite its location outside Europe and Northern America, Israel in the 20th century couldn't afford to expend valuable resources on peacock feathers and elaborate public shows surrounded by existential military threats. Its front end has more resembled the front ends outside of the West where to the extent it exists at all it is to justify the results of the back end. When wars are being fought and terrorists are blowing up buses there is already sufficient "entertainment". In 2025 though, halfway through the 2020s decade, things are most definitely a-changin' globally. Whether it is the Covid pandemic, the Russia-Ukraine war, the Israel-Iran war, mass immigration, a reshaping of global trade with Trump tariffs, a collapse in the legitimacy of global institutions like the United Nations and reassessments on foreign policy that haven't been considered since World War 2 everything is up in the air. Maybe, maybe the United States can still afford the peacock act though its fiscal situation suggests otherwise. But no one else in the West can. When everything is up in the air, including the very viability of your nation state in the 21st century and beyond, peacock front ends don't project strength. Especially when the back end seems to be failing.

As I've already stated the signs are that Israel's back end is not failing, quite the contrary. But the front end is a real concern. In normal times Israel could spend a few years recovering from the national trauma of the October 7th terrorist attacks and the resulting wars. But in the 2020s where the global chess pieces and sands are shifting so rapidly it really can't afford to. Just in 2025 the American Israeli alliance has gone from seemingly ushering in a new golden era of relations and collaboration with the bombing of Iran's nuclear facilities and alignment over the future of Gaza, Judea and Samaria to the complete opposite. It has gone from the Americans rejecting a two state solution at the United Nations to rejecting Israeli sovereignty over that same land, "always" if you believe Vice President Vance. The shopping trolley movements are enough to give one whiplash. The Americans can maybe afford the shopping trolley movements just as it (maybe) can still afford its peacock front end, perhaps Trump has even landed on a deliberate and correct whiplash strategy for American allies and adversaries, but the Israelis cannot afford it. It needs to communicate and implement a coherent strategy if it is to have one other than Netanyahu meekly following Trump's orders as America's new favorite poodle and accepting its place in the pecking order of the American controlled global village. There are zero signs Netanyahu, his administration or perhaps even anyone in the political arena is capable of this. The Israeli media and public conversation is focused on Trump sycophantism after he managed to get some hostages in Gaza back after two years, a total irrelevance in the broader national security and geopolitical trends. The gap between the competence of Israel's front end and the apparent competence of Israel's back end is absolutely yawning and getting bigger. The similarities with the UK in the early 2000s post September 11th terrorist attacks when the UK basked in its special relationship with the United States are freaking me out. I've seen how that story ends. Have I swapped one country with another country that is about to repeat the same mistakes post October 7th terrorist attacks?

If Trump foreign policy can be bought by the highest bidder it really does not bode well for Taiwan. Israel has just engaged multiple surrounding enemies that want to see it wiped out, on its own with very limited American involvement and emerged stronger with a number of military successes. If the United States abandoned Israel after a high bid from a Qatari, Arab consortium it would be deeply concerning and require a swift reorientation that Israel may not be capable of but if the United States abandoned Taiwan after a high bid from China it is hard to see how Taiwan could fend off Chinese advances in the best case scenario. Even Ukraine has largely fought off the Russians in sustained fighting for three years and has the option of surrendering some of its land (Luhansk, Donetsk etc) in a peace deal. Taiwan does not have this option as a small island, nor has it engaged China yet in a hot warfare environment. For the first time in decades the United States has a President seemingly willing to abandon American foreign policy orthodoxy on his volatile shopping trolley expeditions when anything other than a watertight American backstop seems like it would be curtains for Taiwanese aspirations to be a viable independent nation state. The American back end (intelligence services etc) would understand deeply the cost of surrending Taiwanese computer chip fabrication plants to China but it is not clear if a former property developer and former TV celebrity would be as familiar with the technological details, assuming as commander-in-chief he makes the final decision. The option that may be available to Taiwan that isn't available to Israel is a coalition of neighbors (Japan, Philippines, Indonesia etc) grouping together and declaring they will attempt to defend the integrity of the first island chain in East Asia but this currently seems like a pipe dream. If the United States was to abandon the first island chain one would expect that the focus would turn to ensuring the United States reinforced the second island chain and the effective abandonment of Taiwan. An Israel that was smart enough for where the world is possibly headed would be engaging with these issues and thinking through the ramifications: both geopolitical and industrial; to construct a national policy for long term computer chip production and partnerships with Asian countries where beneficial. The Israel of today is squabbling with Trump over whether Turkish troops should be patrolling Gaza or not. (Plot twist: no they shouldn't, that would be like having Chinese troops patrolling the US-Mexico border.) 

## 81 The ultra bullish case for Israel as superpower in the 21st century

"The question is what happens then when Israel controls the Persian Gulf, the Suez, they control this land mass in the center of Asia, Europe and Africa. All these Belt and Road highways and ports and sea routes. The IMEC, the India-Middle East-Europe (Economic) Corridor, all of that will be under their control. I think it is not farfetched to say this is like a play for superpower status. People can say they are a tiny country with a small population. So was Great Britain. Great Britain was a tiny island. In the era of AI and technology and spying... This is something like a global empire, like a King Solomon, every country is coming to pay tribute. They sit in the center of the world island, the crossroads between all the critical minerals, the world's industry and China." Nick Fuentes on Alex Jones' Infowars

"[If] the Israelis prevail and Iran falls we are talking about an era in history where Israel dominates the entire Middle East. They are unchained from the United States... What happens on the other side of the fall of Iran and the total conquest and domination of the Middle East by Israel is that they become the world power." Nick Fuentes on America First

"Society is coming apart, has been coming apart. We are in the age of complexity and we have been for a long time. Whether you call it modernism, postmodernism, the quantum age, people have realized that things are starting to fall apart. What is interesting about the Israelis is they were writing about this in the 1980s. There is a doctrine (A Strategy for Israel in the 1980s) by one of their planners named Oded Yinon, he wrote it for a future Prime Minister of Israel in the 1980s. In that plan they talk about their strategy for the Middle East, in there is talking about Gaza, the West Bank, Syria, Iraq and Iran, their adversaries, but what a lot of people miss... in there they say our big enemy is not the Arabs, it is not even the Soviets that give them weapons, they said the big enemy is this modernism that is coming apart. The reason that we are going to survive is because we are going to be strong. Although we are small and few in number, although we don't have a big country or a lot of territory we are solid, we are together, we have a sense of who we are, we are concrete, defined. Whereas the rest of the world is going to be ripping each other apart over ideology, over ethnicity, all these different cleavages, we are going to be strong... That is going to be the superpower in this century, organization. Who can actually direct and focus the energy of a large group of people effectively... In these big, diverse countries, in this complex globalized world with ideology, few, even a great and large and mighty country like America, can effectively do that anymore. If America comes apart who will be the strong horse...?" Nick Fuentes

It is deeply ironic but the one with the most ambitious vision for Israel in the 21st century, publicly at least, is the American, Catholic, non-Jewish internet celebrity with a talk show on one of the few platforms (Rumble) that isn't censoring him for being antisemitic, racist and far right. In the world that the Singapore Prime Minister Lawrence Wong describes, "a multi-polar world", "a post American order" leaving a "vacuum" that no other country is able or willing to fill, accepting the role of church or synagogue in the American controlled global village and being lectured by the American Vice President on what votes Israel's Parliament (Knesset) can conduct on domestic affairs that aren't a "stupid political exercise", "strange" and offensive to the global village's visiting Vice Emperor is selling Israel short, there's no doubt. But Israel is today, on the front end at least, so far from being able to fulfil anything close to the vision Fuentes puts forward for what Israel could be in the 21st century. It doesn't see itself or project itself as a potential aspiring superpower. The propaganda war exercised on American owned and controlled (funny that?) online platforms since the October 7th terrorist attacks accusing Israel of "genocide", "starvation" and "ethnic cleansing" in Gaza have taken their toll on the national psyche (something that **was** encouraged and whipped up by Fuentes). The obsequiousness displayed whenever an American politician or celebrity visits Israel projects weakness and second class global village citizen status. This is Netanyahu's Israel. Where Israel is dependent on Netanyahu to be a bridge to the United States and hence can't afford to discard Netanyahu at elections. Without that Netanyahu bridge and without the support of the global village's first class citizens flying in for a photo opportunity Israel is not a viable, independent nation state. It is the Middle Eastern Taiwan, just with no neighbors that would consider banding together to fight off the regional hegemon. I personally think Wong's declaration of a post American order is premature even though Trump foreign policy on auction to the highest bidder and Vance trying to project Vice Emperor status in Israel have forced me to reassess my priors. But if you combine the Wong view with the Fuentes view on what Israel could be you can't fail but see the massive opportunity if only Israel could raise its game and actually believe in itself.  

## 82 A Jewish state, if you can keep it

It was the American socialite Elizabeth Willing Powel who according to historical record asked Benjamin Franklin whether he had helped form a republic or monarchy and prompted his famous quote "A republic, if you can keep it." In 2025 it is not obvious that Silicon Valley billionaires or indeed President Trump himself, those with American money and power, care enough about keeping it. There is a personal cost to doing what is right for your country and that cost is vastly elevated during critical times. Pursuing self interest entirely or even partially, cementing your oligopoly or transitioning to trillionaire status from billionaire status, when your country is suffering economic, demographic and ideological convulsions is not going to be sufficient to keep that republic intact. A country in an existential war is not going to win that war if its generals have even half of a mind on pursuing personal wealth in deals with the enemy rather than fighting it. The challenges facing the United States are vast and although there was not a superior or even a serious alternative to Trump and his alliance with the Silicon Valley oligarchs at the ballot box in 2024 it doesn't mean that it is going to be enough. Especially so if those individuals no longer believe in that republic anymore. There is an argument that the republic has already failed or is in the process of doing so. Hence when Peter Thiel's favorite court philosopher Curtis Yarvin argues for an American monarchy and to "end the democratic experiment" at a Yale University debate (October 2025) the audience isn't aghast like Benjamin Franklin and the Founding Fathers no doubt would have been. The America that emerges post Trump is not within Israel's control no matter what the anti Israel conspiracists like Fuentes claim. There is a tendency to be transfixed by the great American drama whether that be the January 6th Capitol riot in 2021, the failed Trump assassination attempts, the successful Charlie Kirk assassination attempt or the election of Islamic socialists like Zohran Mamdani to the position of New York City Mayor but none of this under Israel's control. Israel is under Israel's control assuming it enforces its sovereignty and independence. And it has a Jewish state if it can keep it.

If the focus is long term, post Trump and post Netanyahu, the future is undoubtedly as I stated earlier "the network(ed) state". On the demographic front white (nominally Christian) Europeans are surrendering nation state after nation state in Europe and state after state in the United States. Once surrendered and once the demographic tipping point has been reached the 19th century or 20th century peak version of that (nation) state is never returning. The math on white European birth rates versus non-white non-European birth rates is cruel and inexorable. I witnessed what a decade of a Sadiq Khan mayoralty did to London and you don't have to be a soothsayer to predict what a decade of Zohran Mamdani would do to New York City. Muslim populations concern me more than say Hindu or Buddhist populations for obvious reasons (terrorism, Sharia law, establishing aggressive Islamic caliphates, UK grooming gangs etc) but even more peaceful, more respectful, less aggressive populations change the character and values of a (nation) state. India or China, for all their strengths and weaknesses, are qualitatively and quantitatively different to 20th century America or 19th century Britain. Once a (nation) state is majority Indian or Chinese it will obviously increasingly resemble a Little India or Little China rather than a 20th century America or 19th century Britain. On the fiscal front a sustainable national debt path is being surrendered. As of October 2025 the United States national debt is 38 trillion dollars (125 percent of GDP) and inexorably rising. As I write this the federal government is shutdown, not because either side wants to reverse this fiscal trend but because one side wants to increase it faster than the other. Short of a great American rug pull redenominating the national debt in Bitcoin rather than the US dollar it is not a question of whether the United States will default or inflate its debt away, it is a question of when. So when the majority of the states in the United States are permanently non-white, non-Christian, non-European, left wing or socialist leaning and the federal government is paralyzed, dsyfunctional and essentially bankrupt what are the states (e.g. Florida, Texas) that still resemble success stories to do? Just like Israel in the Middle East they have to erect barriers to protect themselves from the regional majority and a federal government that will undoubtedly go back to a Democrat President at some point seeking the non-white, non-Christian, non-European vote. Just like Israel in the Middle East they have to control their immigration policy to ensure a future Democrat President opening the national borders to yet more third world immigration doesn't change the demographics of their states. Just like Israel in the Middle East they have to look for allies and trade relationships halfway around the globe rather than relying on the basket case neighbor state next door. Just like Israel in the Middle East they have to aggressively protect the identity, economic overperformance and fiscal position of their state even if it means national and global unpopularity, propaganda campaigns smearing their reputation and accusations of racist and religious superiority. Those states with significant Christian Zionist and Jewish populations will have a willing and enthusiastic ally waiting for them in the Middle East. This isn't the United States that the Founding Fathers sought or dreamed about but the numbers both demographically and fiscally are horrible and only going in one direction.

Israel's demographic and fiscal numbers aren't as concerning as the United States', as a small country without the world's reserve currency and without the precedent of being the 20th century's pre-eminent global superpower they simply can't afford to be. But if you scratch below the headline numbers there are certainly long term challenges if not reasons for concern. On the demographic front Israel is the outlier amongst the West in that it has a growing native (Jewish) population and doesn't need to prop up its GDP economic growth numbers and the projected solvency of its social security schemes by swelling its population with immigrants. Its birth rate was 2.9 children per woman in 2023 which compares to the United States' 1.62, the United Kingdom's 1.56 and the OECD average of 1.5, all below replacement rate. As discussed earlier this is primarily driven by the Haredi (or ultra-Orthodox) segment of the Jewish population which averages up to 7 children per woman and is projected to reach a third of the Israeli population by 2050. In an ideal world Israeli political discourse would be focused on the long term challenge the exponentially growing Haredi population presents. In the actual world the Trump, Netanyahu, American, Arab coalition ensures more pressing problems such as Gaza, Judea and Samaria are never resolved and so this particular issue repeatedly gets kicked into the long grass. Long term the Haredi population could make or break the Jewish state on a number of different axes. The obvious axis is defense. A small country with a population of approximately 10 million does not have a large pool of reservists to mobilize to begin with once you factor in age and to a more limited extent gender. If you grant exemptions to a third of the population (Haredis) and a fifth of the population (Arabs) that potential pool shrinks even further. The modern day nation state of Israel has been blessed by an era in which defense isn't purely a numbers game as technological superiority allows smaller militaries to fight off and in some cases defeat much larger ones. It has also been blessed by an era in which its much more populous Arab enemies haven't been aligned on military strategy and haven't capitalized during brief points in time when Israel's defenses were truly reeling such as at the beginning of the Yom Kippur War in 1973 or indeed in the days following the October 7th 2023 terrorist attacks. The typical Haredi perspective might be that Hashem will protect Israel if enough Haredis pray and that the human endeavor ensuring technological superiority and a competent, well organized fighting force is next to irrelevant. The Orthodox perspective, let alone the secular perspective, may take umbrage with this claim. However, the Haredi population not only presents a defense challenge it is also presents an economic one. After being on the absolute floor experiencing hyperinflation in the 1980s Israel's economy has grown to a GDP (gross domestic product) of approximately 540 billion USD in 2024 or half an Elon Musk assuming he becomes a trillionaire in the near future. (Let's leave for now the discussion of whether one man can credibly be considered twice as valuable as Israel's entire economy.) This is relatively healthy although when you look at GDP per capita (GDP divided by its population) it is less impressive. Israel had a GDP per capita of approximately 54,000 USD in 2024 which compares to the United States' 86,000 USD or Singapore's 91,000 USD. The United Kingdom had a similar GDP per capita as Israel at 53,000 USD. This essentially means that the United States and Singapore have almost double the average economic output per person when compared to Israel. Does this matter? Can the Holy Land or the global village's church/synagogue really be expected to compete economically with the United States and Singapore? Can you put a price on the societal contributions of spiritual leaders like "The Rebbe", "The Rambam" or Rabbi Meir Kahane? Perhaps not. But when the significant and growing Haredi population refuses to complete military service so they can contribute to Israel's defense, refuses to offer a (partially) secular education to their children so they can contribute to Israel's economy in the world of atoms or the world of bits and refuses to accept that millions of Haredi can't all be serving rabbis let alone reach the heights of a rare individual like "The Rebbe" you start to appreciate that below the headline birth rate numbers there isn't much to be optimistic about. You would much rather have an Haredi problem than an importing third world immigrants problem to inflate the population numbers. But it could increasingly be a millstone around Israel's neck nonetheless militarily and economically. In the worst case scenario of Haredi voters teaming up with Arab voters they could by 2050 have a majority to vote in a coalition that brings the entire state crashing down. Theodor Herzl, David Ben-Gurion and Ze'ev Jabotinsky brought into being a Jewish state but it is up to today's Jews to ensure they keep it.

"The Haredi world is right that Torah protects. Hazal (חז״ל), the sages, say Torah shields and saves. But the Torah never meant for prayer and learning to replace action. It meant for faith to guide action. When Amalek attacked, Joshua (יהושע) fought while Moses (משה) prayed. The Torah tells us that Israel prevailed only when Moses' hands were lifted towards heaven and Joshua's soldiers fought below. Neither faith alone nor action alone was enough. That's the model. Torah and defense. Heaven and earth. Body and soul. Each complementing the other. So yes, Torah protects the soldiers but the soldiers are also the way Hashem channels that protection into the world. Torah provides spiritual merit and the soldiers through their mesirut nefesh (מסירת נפש), through their sacrifice, their courage, they create their own immense merit too. Both are expressions of divine service. One through study and prayer, the other through sacrifice and action. Without Torah our defense lacks soul, without defenders our Torah lacks a vessel to live in. They are not rivals, they are partners. That is why gratitude must go both ways. No one in Jewish history has ever supported Torah study like the modern state of Israel. Tens of billions of shekels have gone into yeshivas, stipends, housing, food programs, child care. Maybe it wasn't always given enthusiastically. But if someone funds your institutions and protects your streets for decades reluctance doesn't erase generosity. And if we use the state's hospitals, roads and security we are stakeholders in that state whether we sing Hatikvah (Israeli national anthem) or not. The Torah commands hakarat hatov (הכרת הטוב, recognizing the good), gratitude, as a sacred duty. If Moses could show gratitude even to the Nile, how much more must we show gratitude to the people and structures that allow Torah to flourish in Israel today? And indeed that support has helped Torah flourish like never before. Think about it. Under Ottoman or British rule there were hardly any yeshivas and certainly not thriving in the way they are now. No safety for Jews to live in as they do today. Only when there was a Jewish state, defended by Jewish soldiers, could Torah return to Eretz Israel in such strength. For the first time in 2000 years Torah is being learned on a massive scale in the land of Israel. Because Jewish soldiers made it possible. The body protects the soul and the soul gives meaning to the body. Each exists for the other." Oliver Anisfeld, J-TV

There is an interesting parallel when you compare the split between Christian Zionists and the anti Israel contingent in the Republican Party in the United States and the split between the Orthodox and the Haredi in Israel over what the modern day nation state of Israel represents. To the Christian Zionists the return of Jews to the land of Israel is an exciting fulfillment of bibical prophecy and evidence that G\*d's original covenant with the Jewish people was never broken or replaced. Rather than threatening their Christian beliefs or bringing into question their own covenant with G\*d they perceive it as being strengthened when the "olive tree" they were grafted into to "share in the nourishing sap from the olive root" (Romans 11:17-18) is shown to be standing strong. They believe that branches were "broken off because of unbelief" but that those newly grafted in "do not support the root, but the root supports [them]". The Christians amongst the anti Israel contingent, obviously there are many secular and Muslim individuals within this contingent too, are broadly in the supersessionist camp. They believe that the covenant with the Jewish people was broken and replaced with a new covenant with the Christians, essentially that the "olive tree" was broken and fell and a new olive tree was grown in its place. Hence evidence that the original covenant with the Jewish people still stands and that there is a role in biblical prophecy for Jews that didn't convert to Christianity is deeply threatening to their religious doctrine. As former Fox News host Tucker Carlson stated in an interview with the Texas Senator Ted Cruz the modern day nation state of Israel is merely a "political entity", a secular state "run by Benjamin Netanyahu". What does this rupture in an American political party have to do with the split between the Orthodox and the Haredi within Israel itself? Just like the supersessionist Christians in America the Haredi are uncomfortable with what the modern day nation state of Israel represents. Whether it is because the Jewish Moshiach (Messiah) hasn't arrived yet, because the Zionists that formed the state like Herzl, Ben-Gurion and Jabotinsky were broadly secular, because the Declaration of Independence made no direct reference to Hashem or because cities like Tel Aviv are considered too secular the reverence they display for the Torah is not shared for the land and the modern day Jewish nation state that stands today on that land. The land that was justifiably fought over and defended in the Torah multiple times is, not yet at least, worth fighting for and defending in the present day. A Haredi Tucker Carlson is no doubt as I write this telling fellow Jews that the nation state in which they reside is a "political entity" and a secular state "run by Benjamin Netanyahu" and that they should fight to the death, not to defend it but to resist contributing to its defense. It is a rather sad, circular argument. Of course if the religious Jews perceive the modern day Jewish state as something unholy, not resembling the Israel of the Torah, not worth contributing to and defending and something foreign or alien to Hashem it will forever remain so. It can only be something holy, resembling the Israel of the Torah and worth contributing to and defending when you perceive it as such and decide to treat it as such. After all, the land is the same land as in the Torah (admittedly with smaller borders currently, regrettably), the people that inhabit the land are broadly distant descendants of the same people in the Torah, Hashem is the same Hashem as in the Torah and the (written) Torah hasn't changed since the times of the Torah. All the pieces are there. 

## 83 Super Sparta

"Israel is in a sort of isolation. We will increasingly need to adapt to an economy with autarkic characteristics, the word I most hate. I am a believer in the free market but we may find ourselves in a situation where our arms industries are blocked. We will need to develop arms industries here - not only research and development, but also the ability to produce what we need. We are Athens and Sparta. But we're going to be Athens and super-Sparta. There's no choice; in the coming years, at least, we will have to deal with these attempts to isolate us. What's worked until now will not work from now on." Benjamin Netanyahu (September 16th 2025)

It is rare in recent times to hear anything from Netanyahu's mouth that can't be imputed to either self-aggrandizement, public relations or dutifully carrying out the role of Trump stooge but to his credit the occasional smoke signal is emitted that suggests there is still a semblance of long term strategic thinking rather than an exclusive focus on political self-preservation. One example that went under the radar was his response to a journalist's question on what book he was currently reading, "A book by a historian, by the name of Barry Strauss. It's called The Jews [vs] Rome. Jews against Rome.... We lost that one. We have to win the next one." One example that very much detonated above the radar was his public declaration at a Ministry of Finance conference that due to defense and geopolitical realities Israel would need to become a "super-Sparta". The wailing and gnashing of teeth, inevitably from opposition politicians and hostile Israeli media but more disappointingly also from technology leaders and less hostile Israeli media, led to Netanyahu partially walking the statement back the next day. Avi Hasson, CEO of Startup Nation Central, the non-profit that recently released an exceptional report on "Israel in the Global Semiconductor Race" (more on that later) had responded "It's an unacceptable vision. No one is buying that [super-Sparta vision], as it's irrelevant for Israel. Israel is not a superpower like China or the US - our economy as a whole relies on raw materials, and certainly for our tech economy, global connectivity is like our oxygen." The major Tel Aviv Stock Exchange indices had also fallen between 1-2 percent in the immediate aftermath of Netanyahu's comments. With technological visionaries like these who needs Luddite lemmings?

Let's start with what Netanyahu clearly didn't mean when he referred to a 21st century (super) Sparta because unfortunately stating the obvious seems to be necessary. (I should perhaps be more charitable to Hasson and the like, Israelis have been under siege for two years both literally and figuratively and that isn't conducive to rational, long term thinking.) A 21st century Sparta, or indeed any nation state or superpower with adversaries, would not last very long if it refused to acquire the raw materials (e.g. aluminium, iron, copper, steel, lithium, titanium etc) it needed for defense or had zero leverage over global trade partners to acquire them. Netanyahu was not suggesting that Israel limit itself going forward to the raw materials that are present within its currently tiny borders. Nor was Netanyahu suggesting that Israel cut all the fiber optic submarine communications cables that connect it to the global internet and go back to purely paper based systems. Sparta was a leading military force over two millennia ago but would struggle to defend itself today against the tin-pot dictator of a failed state (UK? Jokes....) without access to modern day technology. So what events and forces led Netanyahu to summon the spirit of ancient Sparta? The dependence on the United States is repeatedly setting off alarm bells in the Israeli national security establishment. Whether it is President Biden or President Trump or numerous predecessors threatening arms embargoes it is clear that if Israel has any kind of aspiration to have the ability to complete critical military objectives rather than repeatedly leaving them unfulfilled it can't afford to continue to follow American orders ad infinitum. And yet whilst Israel is solely dependent on the United States for supplying missile interceptors and key components of its air defense systems it has to limit itself to muttering obscure ancient history references in public and humiliating apology calls to whoever recently provided President Trump with a free Boeing 747. Threatened arms embargoes from the Americans are nothing new but President Trump is managing to set off novel alarms that none of his predecessors managed. Selling F-35 stealth fighter jets to Saudi Arabia and potentially other Arab neighbors has the potential to erode Israel's air superiority in the region and pushes Israel to work on F-35 upgrades in secret without sharing them with the United States. Trump may be blinded by the dollar signs but to Israel their technological edge is a matter of life or death. On a long enough time frame America's pre-eminent superpower status is dependent on it too.

The major upside to Israel is that it is being forced, perhaps prematurely, to face and address issues that a multitude of nation states around the world will have to face themselves sooner or later. Whoever has the technological edge and whoever has already found answers to the questions that the 21st century poses will have more than enough leverage to obtain the raw materials it needs in trade negotiations. All the noise, all the social media propaganda, all the infiltration and delegitimization of global institutions like the United Nations, all the arrest warrants issued on trumped up charges of genocide, all of it fades into insignificance if another nation state looks at Israel and sees in it the difference between winning or losing their future war and the difference between being able to defend itself or not being able to defend itelf. But that aforementioned nation state will only look at Israel that way if it is credibly not a vassal state of the United States. If it is merely a vassal state of the United States then whatever technological edge or answers Israel can provide can be obtained by going through and dealing with the United States. Israel is obviously observing, monitoring and lobbying against American sales of the F-35 fighter jet to its Arab neighbors but is it the only nation or city state with an interest in maintaining an element of air superiority in its region? Of course not. For example, Singapore ordered four F-35Bs in 2020 for 2.75 billion USD and eight more F-35Bs in 2023 that are due to arrive in 2026-2028 (defensenews.com). It will no doubt be looking on with great interest at how the United States approaches sales in the Middle East and to what extent Israel is allowed to maintain air superiority by the Americans or how Israel is able to maintain air superiority despite the Americans.

Israel already has a jump-start on this particular problem. As early as 2010 Israel entered into negotiations with the United States for the purchase of F-35 fighter jets on the condition that it could make its own modifications and customizations to the aircraft. Although these initial changes were limited it ensured Israel became the first country and to this day only country (publicly at least) to be granted such permissions. Multiple iterations since, over more than a decade, have resulted in the F-35I or the "Adir" (אדיר, mighty one) with a unique information system, next generation electronic warfare, integration of Israeli weapon systems, external fuel tanks and the ability to carry weapons under its wings (Wall Street Journal). The United States reportedly still locks down the internal core system but Israel, with today's plug and play architecture, is able to add capabilities such as experimental precision missiles and command, control, communications and computing (C4) systems without waiting for American approval and going through Pentagon bureaucracy (Tactical Sky YouTube channel). Even in the highly unlikely case that Israel's Arabs neighbors managed to obtain the exact same state of the art aircraft as the Israelis, the F-35I say, there are still the matter of potential kill switches, access to software updates, maintenance challenges, pilot training and the need to acquire spare parts. But the air dominance Israel displayed during the Twelve Day War with Iran could, temporarily at least, be eroded with enemy aircraft able to detect Israeli fighter jets in the sky when their air defense system fails to trigger. A 21st century (super) Sparta, short of designing, sourcing the materials for and manufacturing a totally new fighter jet from scratch, controlling every aspect of the entire system, couldn't aspire to be much more Spartan.
